## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator with state (x,v) evolving in time t, which is the standard phase-space form of second-order ODEs x'' = f(x,v,t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly combine a restoring force depending on x, damping depending on v, and possibly time-dependent (driven/parametric) terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- State-space identity: dv_dt = f(x, v, t) (general second-order oscillator written as first-order system)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative restoring force)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper oscillator)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Higher-order stiffness/potential expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (polynomial restoring force from nonlinear potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent dissipation, aerodynamic-like drag at larger |v|)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, positive damping at large |x|; self-excited limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-based self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (limit-cycle generation via nonlinear damping in v)
- Liénard-type oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4) * v (general nonlinear damping as an even function of x)
- Driven oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical chaotic/nonlinear resonance model)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness, Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance when modulation matches natural frequency)
- Conservative potential form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) (interpretable as dv_dt = -dU/dx with U(x)=c0 * x**2 + c1 * x**4)
- Non-smooth/friction-like dissipation (smoothed): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (Coulomb friction approximation without discontinuity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillation (no dissipation/drive) typically implies dv_dt depends on x only (and is independent of t and v), often as an odd function of x for symmetric potentials.
- Linear damping manifests as a term proportional to v with negative sign; if the fitted v-term changes sign with state (e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v), it suggests self-excitation and possible limit cycles.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is often indicated by the sign of the x**3 term in dv_dt (positive x**3 coefficient in restoring force increases frequency with amplitude; negative decreases it).
- Presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt indicates external periodic forcing; resonance/beat phenomena occur when the forcing frequency is near the natural frequency.
- Time-multiplying stiffness-like terms (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicate parametric modulation, a hallmark of Mathieu/parametric resonance behavior.
- Velocity odd nonlinearities (v**3, v*|v| approximations) suggest drag/friction mechanisms whose dissipation grows rapidly with speed, changing decay rate with amplitude.
- Even-in-x modulation of damping (e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v) suggests amplitude-dependent dissipation, often used to model internal friction or Liénard systems.
- If dv_dt can be written approximately as -dU/dx - c*v, then trajectories tend to follow energy decay; identifying a polynomial in x alone is a cue to reconstruct an effective potential U(x).

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
-2.45151654379511\,x^3\;+\;0.340325443007139\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.826056547542989\,v\;-\;0.413028273771494\,\log(|v|+1)
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Must contain a \(\log(|v|+1)\) term (absolute value is essential; \(v\) can be negative).
- Must contain a linear \(v\) term.
- Must contain an \(x^3\) term (no other powers of \(x\)).
- Must contain a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (phase/scale inside sine can be adjusted via constants).
- No extra terms like \(v^2\), \(x\), \(x^2\), \(x^5\), \(\exp(\cdot)\), \(\log(\text{something not }|v|+1)\), etc., unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–15, 18–35, 39–44
All of these are sums of algebraic terms in \(x\), \(v\), and \(\sin(c_2 t+c_3)\), but **none contains any logarithm**. Since the GT has a nonzero \(-0.4130\log(|v|+1)\) term, these candidates cannot match for all \(v\). Setting parameters cannot create a log term from polynomials/sines.  
Therefore **1–15, 18–35, 39–44 do not match**.

(Also, many include extra terms like \(v^{c}\), \(v^2\), \(x\), etc.; while some could be zeroed out, the missing log already makes them impossible.)

### Candidate 16
\[
c_0 x^3 + c_1\sin(c_2 t+c_3) + c_4\log(c_5 v+1)+c_6 + c_7 v^{c_8}+c_9 v + v
\]
Has a log, but it is \(\log(c_5 v+1)\) **without** \(|v|\). Because \(v\) takes negative values, there is no choice of constants making \(\log(c_5 v+1)\equiv \log(|v|+1)\) for all real \(v\). (They differ for negative \(v\); also domains differ.)  
So **cannot match**.

### Candidate 17
\[
\cdots + c_4\log(c_5 t+1)+\cdots
\]
Log is in \(t\), not \(v\). GT log depends on \(|v|\). **Cannot match**.

### Candidates 36, 45, 47, 49, 50
Contain \(\exp(\cdot)\), extra \(x^5\), or other non-GT structures. Even if you set some coefficients to 0, these candidates still **do not provide \(\log(|v|+1)\)** (they have no log at all). Hence **cannot match**.

### Candidate 37
Has \(\log(c_5 x+1)\) and \(x^5\). Wrong log variable and extra \(x^5\). Even if \(x^5\) coefficient could be zeroed (it cannot; it’s a fixed \(+x^5\) term), it still wouldn’t match the required \(\log(|v|+1)\). **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 38
Has \(\log(c_5 t+1)\) and \(+v^2\) (fixed). Wrong log dependence and extra \(v^2\). **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 40
Has \(+v^2\) (fixed). GT has no \(v^2\). Cannot remove it. **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 41, 42
Each has \(+v^2\) (fixed). Same issue. **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 43, 44
Each has \(+v^2\) (fixed). Same issue. **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 46
Has \(+x^5\) (fixed) and \(x^2\) term. GT has no \(x^5\). Cannot remove. **Cannot match**.

### Candidate 48
\[
c_0 x^3 + c_1\sin(c_2 t+c_3) + c_4\log(c_5 v+1) + c_6 v^{c_7} + c_8 v + c_9 + x^5
\]
Has a log in \(v\) but not \(|v|\), and also has a fixed \(+x^5\) term that cannot be eliminated. Either issue alone prevents equivalence. **Cannot match**.

---

**Overall decisive obstruction:** None of the candidates contains the exact \(\log(|v|+1)\) structure required by the GT. The only log-bearing candidates use \(\log(c_5 v+1)\) (no absolute value) or log of \(t\) or \(x\), and some also include non-removable \(x^5\) or \(v^2\) terms. Because \(v\) can be negative, \(\log(c_5 v+1)\) cannot be made globally identical to \(\log(|v|+1)\) by parameter choice.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO26)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.826056547542989*v - 2.45151654379511*x**3 - 0.413028273771494*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.340325443007139*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x**3` term
2. `sin(t)` term
3. `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term
4. `v` (linear) term

Key observation: The GT contains `log(Abs(v) + 1)`, which involves an absolute value. Since `v` takes both positive and negative values, this is NOT equivalent to `log(v + 1)` or any power of `v`.

Let me analyze the candidates. Most candidates have the form with `v**c` terms instead of `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. A power function `v**c` is fundamentally different from `log(Abs(v) + 1)` - they are linearly independent basis functions. Also, `v**c` for non-integer `c` isn't even defined for negative `v` (which occurs in this domain).

**Candidates 1-15, 18-35, 39-44:** These contain `v**c` terms (power functions of v) but no `log` term. Since `log(Abs(v) + 1)` cannot be expressed as a finite combination of power functions of `v`, these are all **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 16:** `c0*x**3 + c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*log(c5*v + 1) + c6 + c7*v**c8 + c9*v + v`
This has `log(c5*v + 1)`, but the GT has `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. Since `v` takes both signs, `log(c5*v + 1)` ≠ `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 17:** Has `log(c5*t + 1)` - wrong variable in log. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 36-38, 45-50:** These contain `exp`, `log(c5*t+1)`, `log(c5*x+1)`, `log(c5*v+1)`, `sin(c5*v+c6)`, `x**5`, `exp(c5*x)`, `x**c7` terms. 

- **Candidate 36:** Has `exp(c5*v)` and `x**5` - can set c4=0 to kill exp, but x**5 cannot be eliminated. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 37:** Has `log(c5*x+1)` and `x**5`. Wrong log argument. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 38:** Has `log(c5*t+1)` and `v**2`. Wrong log argument. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 45:** Has `exp(c5*x)` and `x**5`. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 46:** Has `x**5`, `x**2` terms. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 47:** Has `exp(c5*v)` and `x**5`. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 48:** `c0*x**3 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*log(c5*v+1) + c6*v**c7 + c8*v + c9 + x**5`. Has `x**5` which can't be eliminated. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 49:** Has `exp(c5*v)` and `x**c7`. Could set c4=0, c6*x**c7 with c7=3 gives x**3 (redundant with c0*x**3). But no log term. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 50:** Has `sin(c5*v+c6)` and `x**5`. **NO MATCH**.

None of the candidates contain `log(Abs(v) + c)` which is essential for matching the GT. The `log(c5*v + 1)` in candidates 16 and 48 doesn't work because `v` takes both signs, making `Abs(v)` fundamentally different from `v`.
